Here's a summary of what was created:\n\n## Summary\n\n### `src/Compilers/CSharp/Portable/Binder/UnifiedSymbolResolver.cs`\n\nA new file implementing the unified symbol resolution strategy pattern with:\n\n- **`SymbolResolutionResult`** — captures found `Symbols` (`ImmutableArray<Symbol>`) and `Diagnostics` (`ImmutableArray<Diagnostic>`), with a `HasSymbols` convenience property and a static `Empty` sentinel.\n\n- **`ISymbolResolutionStrategy`** — interface with a single `LookupInSingleScope()` method that applies a lookup policy at one binder scope.\n\n- **`TypeResolutionStrategy`** — singleton strategy that constrains lookups to namespaces/types (`LookupOptions.NamespacesOrTypesOnly`), used for type-resolution contexts.\n\n- **`MemberAccessResolutionStrategy`** — per-instance strategy that holds a `Qualifier` (`NamespaceOrTypeSymbol`) for member access contexts.\n\n- **`NamespaceResolutionStrategy`** — singleton strategy for namespace resolution (also uses `NamespacesOrTypesOnly`).\n\n- **`UnifiedSymbolResolver`** — wraps a root `Binder` and exposes a `Resolve(name, arity, strategy, options)` method that walks the binder scope chain using the given strategy, mirrors the two-pass (no-diagnose then diagnose) fallback pattern from `Binder.LookupSymbolsInternal`.\n\n### `src/Compilers/CSharp/Test/Semantic/Semantics/UnifiedSymbolResolverTests.cs`\n\nNine `[Fact]` tests covering:\n- `SymbolResolutionResult.Empty` behavior\n- Construction with real symbols and diagnostics\n- Default `ImmutableArray` handling\n- Singleton identity for `TypeResolutionStrategy` and `NamespaceResolutionStrategy`\n- Qualifier storage in `MemberAccessResolutionStrategy`\n- `UnifiedSymbolResolver.Resolve()` returning non-null results for both found and not-found cases\n- Interface assignability of all concrete strategies\n- Arity variation
